   1. EXTENT OF IMPLEMENTATION OF THE POVERTY REDUCTION
       STRATEGY PAPER

   2. Burluna Faso in 2007 experienced a slowdown in its economic growth rate in real terms
   compared to the last two years (4.0% against 5.5% in 2006 and 7.1% in 2005), as a result of a poor
   crop season due to an unequal spatial and temporal distribution of rainfall and the persistent
   difficulties being faced by the cotton sector .The growth rate for 2007 also dropped by 1.4points
   when compared to the average for UEMOA member countries whch stood at +4.3%. The
   relatively good performance of the economy stems essentially from the performance of the
   secondary and tertiary sectors which respectively recorded a growth rate of +8.3% and +3.5%.

     1.1.        SPEEDING UP OF ECONOMIC GROWTH BASED ON EQUITY

   3.    The State budget remains the most ideal tool for financing PRSP priority actions.
   Consequently, the goal of the Medlum Term Expendture Framework (MTEF), whose sectoral
   c e h g s were used as basis for drawing up the 2008 appropriation law, was poverty alleviation
   aimed at fachtating progress towards the attainment of the Mdlennium Development Goals. Ths
   appropriation law was adopted by the National Assembly in December 2007 with the following
   priorities: 1) enhancement of the fight against poverty; 2) revival of the productive sectors of the
   economy; 3) development of employment; 4) fight against fraud and corruption; 5) strengthening
   of security and promotion of humans rights, 6) further reform of the State and finally; 7)
   implementation of the total communalization of the territory.

   4. As concerns the strategy adopted to overcome the crisis in the cotton sector following the
   decltne in world cotton prices that plunged cotton companies into financial deficits, h s is being
   implemented and is made up among other measures of the following i) recapitahation of cotton
   companies (SOFITEX, SOCOMA, FASO COTON); ii) consolidation of claims by local banks

from SOFITEX totaling CFA F 44 Bdhon; iii) revision of smoothmg mechanism parameters (five-
year moving average) and its use in determining the purchase price of cottonseed during
subsequent seasons; iv) continuation of consultations between the State, AICB, the World Bank
and AFD, in order to render smoothmg funds operational.. It is also noteworthy to mention
Government's decision to re-dsengage from SOFITEX'S capital and the launch of financial and
operational audts of SOFITEX for the 2004-2007 period.

5. In order to revive cotton production, a necessary condtion for attaining financial equhbrium
in the sector, Government increased subsides for inputs from CFA F 3 blllton to 6.5 bdhon to
help maintain the resale price at a level close to that of the previous season, thereby rendering
inputs accessible to producers. Government also agreed with cotton companies, pendmg the
processing of the internal debts of groups, to, in&scriminately, make seeds and inputs available to
all producers, some of whom, due to the effects of the floods of the 2007-2008 season, were
unable to meet their obligations for inputs loans. This effort should reactivate their incentive to
continue producing cotton, after the decline in production by 44% in 2007-2008.

6. Poor clunatic condtions of the 2007-2008 season affected food production in one thwd of the
provinces. The impact of this situation, particularly on the most vulnerable, was compounded by
the hke in the prices of convenience goods, especially foodstuffs. In order to mitigate the short-
term effects, Government took various measures includmg: i) the resale at social prices of cereals
taken from the security stock; ii) suspension for a period of six months, with effect from March
2008, of custom duties and/or VAT on rice, powder mdk, concentrated mdk and salt, and iii) the
close monitoring of price trends and the strengthening of dalogue with importers, wholesalers, to
protect the most vulnerable among the population.

7. In addtion, the design of a national strategy for export promotion, started in 2007 and geared
towards speeding up economic growth, w d continue in 2008.

8. Government continued its efforts to reduce or elmmate administrative obstacles to private
investment. It is withm th~scontext that the special operation to issue land titles, conducted from
Decemberl5,2006 toJanuary 31 2007 in the towns of Ouagadougou and Bobo Dioulasso,was
renewed in 2007 and extended to all regonal headquarters.The 2008 appropriation law adopted in
December 2007 has renewed ths provision and measures are being put in place to make its
implementation easy.

9. The implementation of structural reforms and the improvement of condtions for sustaining
strong economic growth driven by the private sector helped reduce the rigdty index for
employment from 64% in 2006 to 61% in 2007. Measures were also taken in 2007 to reduce the
period of repayment of VAT loans to 90 days at the most. These provisions notably include the
payment of a deposit of 70% of the amount of credt exposure withm ten days of receipt of the
claim and the settlement of the unspent credt balance following the verificationprocedure, and no
later than w i h 90 days.

 10. As regards the improvement of the business clunate, and in order to fac&tate the settingup

 1.2.2     Access to healthservices

1,2.3Accessto dnnking waterand sanitation

20. Access to safe drinlung water remains, despite the encouragmg results obtained in thls area, a
major concern in a poverty reduction context. Actions undertaken by Government in the water
sector and the promotion of hygene and sanitation are geared towards acheving the d e n n i u m

21. Government has, through the Directorate General of Water Resources, begun the process of
contracting water services with the involvement of local authorities in management. Thus,
Government has, as part of the implementation process of the reform of the maintenance of water
supply systems managed in the form of public-private partnershp between rural councils and
professional operators, signed agreements for the transfer of drinkingwater infrastructures in rural
areas for some thtrty drinlung water systems


        1.3 EXPANDINGJOB OPPORTUNITIESAND INCOME-GENERATING
                          ACTIVITIES FOR THE POOR IN EQUITY

22.  Ths thtrd component of the PRSP and its priority reforms program focus on bullding the
income-generating capacities of the poor by promoting their participation in the production
process.

23. In order to ensure visibhty as regards access to land, something very important in the rural
areas, Government, in 2007, adopted a national policy on land security in the rural areas. It then
embarked on a process of consultation with all the stakeholders,with the hope of coming up with
a b d laylngdown the guidelmes on rural lands, to be submitted to Parliament.

24.   As concerns the cotton sector, stdl facing low prices in CFA francs on the world market,
cotton seed production dropped by 44% in 2007. However, measures taken as part of the strategy
for ending the crisis, developed in concert with all the actors and supported in its implementation

by financial and technical partners have helped stabhze the situation and restore confidence
among cotton growers.

25. Government also continued the implementation of actions for the development of income-
generating activities for the most socially vulnerable. The implementation of the action plan of the
national strategy for micro finance, that is enjoying the support of technical and financialpartners,
falls squarely in h e with thts determination to improve the living condtions of the poor.


                           1.4. PROMOTING GOOD GOVERNANCE

26.    Sipficant progress has been made in the area of governance, thanks to improvements in
public finance management mechanisms and the decentralization process whch continued to be
government's top priorities throughout the year 2007. The major actions carried out in this area
were geared towards the consolidation of achevements.

27.    Following the PRGB conducted between 2002 and 2006, Government in February 2007
adopted the Public Finance Enhancement Strategy (SRFP) with the primary goal being the
establishment by 2015 of a more transparent and efficient financial management system,
conforming to international standards The first SRFP three-year sectoral action plan for the period
2007-2010, focuses on three priorities: i) increasing the mobhzation of internal resources; ii)
improving the public procurement process iii) strengthening the monitoring device. The SRFP is
seen by Government as the sole reference framework for carrying out reforms in the area of
public finance.

28. In the public procurement sector, the reforms being carried out are part of the action plan
adopted in 2006 followingthe second analytical review of the public procurement system (CPAR).
During 2007, the major actions, under the implementation of thts plan, concerned the adoption
of two decrees, one creating, defining the duties, and organizing the Public Contracts Regulatory
Board (ARMP) and the other organizing and d e h g the functioning of the Ministry of Finance
and the Budget, whch has created the Directorate General of Public Contracts (DGMP) that has
replaced the former central department and has been endowed with new attributions and
decentralized structures w i h the ministries and regons.

29. As concerns monitoring, capacity bu1ldmg in various areas of the sundry control structures
was the main concern. Consequently, in order to render these bodes more operational, a dozen
vehcles were bought for them. Training activities were carried out under the SRFP action plan or
specific programs supported by certain member partners of the General Organization Framework
of Budgetary Support for the implementation of ~ ~ ~ P R S    It wasPin this vein that measures were
taken to fachtate the implementation of the action program of the public finance supreme audtt
institution, namely, the State Audit Office, firstly, through the release system already in place for
other institutions, and secondly, the adoption of Decree N02008-046relating to the administrative
reconcihationof the management accounts of local authorities.

30. As concerns the fight against corruption, the major action in 2007 was the adoption of the
law setting up the Supreme Audt Authority of the State (ASCE). Ths Authority has in addttion
taken over, not only the functions of the General State Inspectorate and the High Authority
charged with coordmating the fight against corruption, but also a part of the duties of the national
coordmation team charged with combating fraud.. With greater powers than those of the
structures whose attributions it has inherited, notably the power of referral and action, the follow-
up of the recommendations of control bodes and institutions, ASCE has to publish an annual
report on its activities.

31. Government onJune 20,2008 launched the activities of the Initiative for Transparencyin the
Extractive Industries in Burhna Faso, whch it expressed its intention to adhere to in 2007. The
Government's intention here is to ensure transparency in the management of mining activities at
h s stage when the sector is fully developing in Burkma Faso. An institutional arrangement
involving all stakeholders as well as the c i d society was established to monitor activities to be
undertaken under h s framework. To date, the start-up phase of the Initiative is nearing
completion with the drawing up of the draft action plan to be validated during a workshop before
the end of the current year.

 32. Regardmg the decentralizationprocess, progress has been made with the adoption of various
texts, notably the decree laying down the standard rules of procedure for local authority councils,
and that on the transfer of powers and resources to urban councils in the areas of preschool,
primary education, health, culture, youths, sports and recreation. For 2008, what wdl be required
wdl be to ensure that these transfers have effectively been carried out, whde clearly defining,
w i h the context of the agreements to be signed with the local authorities their responsibhties so
as to enable each actor to exercise the powers transferred with the resources required. The
k s t r y of the Economy and Finance has, in order to ensure the effective support of the process,
equally carried out the devolution of the services of most of the major directorates such as the
DGTCP, the DGI, the DGB, the DGCF and the DGMP. In h s regard, one may, inter a h ,
mention the creation of new regional treasuries and tax &visions, the training of local council staff
in the use of local authorities integrated accounting software (CICL) and the adoption of a
timetable for the deployment of the CICL administrativemanagement module in 2009.

33.   In order to ensure a more effective monitoring of welfare expendttures and allow a more
complete coverage of the efforts made by government in the fight against poverty, a functional
classification of expendttures accompanied by a codfication of welfare expenditures has been
introduced in the IDC. Thls codificationis being refined to take into account welfare expendtures
not covered but found in inter-ministerial common expenses as a result of centralization of their
settlement.


2. PROSPECTS FOR THE 2008- 2009 PERIOD.

 34. Government wdl continue to make efforts to render operational the poverty reduction
strategypaper, whde strengthening dtaloguewith partners involved in the process.


               2.1    SPEEDING UP ECONOMIC GROWTH BASED O N EQUITY

35. At the macroeconomic level, the second review of the program supported by the PRGF
conducted in March/April2008 reiterated the need to continue the implementation of the actions
indcated in the three major priorities of the PSRS (control system, public procurement and
domestic tax) in order to consolidate public finances and the foundations of economic growth. As
regards the last aspect, emphasis wdl be laid on promoting the private sector and improving the
competitiveness of the economy, particularly through the development, under the sectoral policy
for the Ministry of Trade, a national policy on quality aimed at establishmg a national system of
standardtzation, certification and accredttation for products from Burluna Faso so as to improve
their access to the international market.

36. Government wdl continue to implement the strategy for overcoming the crisis and for
reviving the cotton sector, notably by setting up a framework for consultation between industry

players wherein information can be shared on the status of implementation of the strategy to end
the crisis. Such a framework wdl also serve as a forum for exchanges on the cotton sector
environment and on how the cotton sector can strictly apply the rules governing fund s m o o h g
and determine the floor prices of cotton seed and possible discounts for the 2008-2009 season.
Measures aimed at improving corporate governance and efficiency will also be taken by
SOFITEX, in order to increase its attractiveness to potential investors through notably: i)
continuation of the implementation of the plan to reduce its operating costs; ii) submission of
audted accounts for 2008 with fewer reservations compared to the audted accounts for 2007; iii)
its evaluation by a rating agency.

37. As concerns the improvement of the business clunate, Government wdl carry out several
activities during the year 2008. Indeed, it will lend support to the Burkma "Maison de IEntrepriseY'
through the devolution of Business Formalities Centers (CEFORE) in the North and Central-East
regons and the creation of Centers for the Fachtation of Bu~ldmgDocuments (CEFAC), so as to
improve the provision of services to businesses and, more generally, the business environment in
terms of greater simplification of procedures and reduction of the a h s t r a t i v e costs involved in
running a business.

 38. In the field of food security, Government intends to continue its efforts to ensure food
security for its population. In addtion to the annual appropriation earmarked in the budget for
replenishtng the security stock and the proper functioning of the information system on food
security and nutrition (CFA F 1.45 bfion), government has developed a food security program
aimed at increasing grain production. Special emphasis wdl be laid, in h s regard, on the
development of rice growing plains and the intensification of off-season cultivation. As concerns
the rice sub-program, Government has bought fertdizers for a total amount of CFA F 5 bdhon
and dstributed them to producers.


     2.2. ENSURING ACCESS BY THE POOR TO BASIC SOCIAL SERVICES AND
                                     SOCIAL PROTECTION

39. To acheve its goal of poverty reduction, Government wdl continue to carry out actions in
favor of the poorest by providmg the social sectors with the relevant resources.

40. In the education sector, Government w 4 with the support of its partners in the sector, start
with the implementation of phase I1 of the PDDEB, basing its efforts in this regard, as in phase I,
on the programming framework that the 2009-2011 MTEF education sector represents. Ths wdl
be constantly updated on a gradual basis. The policy of free basic education in the public sector
wdl also be pursued, in conformity with the orientation law thereon.

41. The effectiveness of the decentralization process of the social sectors, already begun in 2007,
wdl experience sipficant breakthroughs with: i) the inclusion in the 2009 appropriation law of
financial resources allocated to local authorities for recurrent expenses (in the area of basic
education) and for rehabhtation investments (in the area of water supply and sanitation), covering
infrastructures and charges related to the powers transferred; ii)     the adoption of operation
arrangements for the management of the services transferred to local authorities in at least 49
urban councils for basic education and to 100 rural councils for drinking water supply, iii) the
transfer of resources programmed for the construction of school fachties to 13 (hteen)
headquarter councils of regons from 2009.

42. In the health sector, the work to do here wdl be to improve quality and efficiency in the use
of health service resources and the updating of the 2009-2011 MTEF. Government wdl also

continue its program of free vaccination for pregnant women and chddren of 0 to 5 years of age
and increase its allocations for delivery and emergency obstetric care.


       2.3    EXPANDING JOB OPPORTUNITIES AND INCOME-GENERATING
                          ACTIVITIES FOR THE POOR IN EQUITY

43.   The momentum already gathered through the adoption of the national policy on securing
lands in the rural areas will be pursued with the preparation of a bdl on rural land tenure following
consultations with all the stakeholders concerned. Special efforts wdl also be made to encourage
self-employmentby youths through the establishment of a mentoring and support fachty for their
project initiatives.

44. Government, in a bid to tackle the escalation in the prices of convenience goods, in particular
cereals, has, with the support of all its partners, pledged to make available to all producers
ferthzers and seeds for the crop year 2008-2009. All the measures taken are aimed at increasing
supply and, generally speaktng,constitute part of the effort to achieve food security.


                          2.4    PROMOTING GOOD GOVERNANCE

45     As concerns good governance, Government remains committed to the effective
implementation of decentrahation, as it is essential for the promotion of participation of the
population at the grass roots in Burkina Faso's development. It thus intends to strengthen the
process, notably by catchmg up with the delays in the transfer of powers and resources to local
authorities. In addtion, it wdl ensure that the standmg development funds for local authorities
created in 2007 to support local authorities' priorityves&nts          go operational, through the
transfer of a least CFA F 5 bdhon in the amended 2008 appropriation law and the allocation in the
2009 appropriation law of at least 5 bdhon for the FPDCT. On a global level, Government wdl, in
a bid to foster transparency in public administration, endeavor to promote e-governance and good
governance in transactions within the administration, and efficiently implement its public
administrationdevolution strategy aimed at strengthening the decentralization process.

 46. As regards reforms in the area of public finance, efforts wdl focus on the implementation of
the activities of the 2008 package of the three-year sectoral action plans of the strategy for
strengthening public finances (SRFP), notably by capitalizing on the achevements already made
through dialogue w i t h the CGAB-PRSP to maintain budgetary aid flows needed to sustain the
implementation of the PRSP priority actions program.

47. Indeed, as concerns the CGAB        - PRSP, the program of activities adopted for 2008 aims at
consolidating dalogue between government and member partners, in connection with the
implementation of the strategy for reducing poverty and promoting better practices in budgetary
support. Budgetary support estimates stood at CFA F 119.2 bdhon in 2008 as against the 116.9
bdhon raised in 2007.

48. The budget design process wdl also continue to be refined in order to ensure a closer h k
with the PRSP process. Government in h s regard has recently adopted a program to reform the
budgetary process, with the aim being the full implementation of the program budget by 2012.
During the transitional phase, it w d continue the process of appropriating programming tools and
experiment the laws of programs with certain key sector ministries. As regards public
procurement, priority will be gven to rendering operational the new sectors created (ARMP and

DGMP) as well as the public procurement information system. Ths will help improve the
procurement system.

49. As concerns enhancement of transparency in the public finance management system, certain
essential budgetary end accounting information wdl be made available on the website of the
Ministry of the Economy and Finance.

50. Government wdl continue the restructuring of the fachty for the fight against corruption,
notably by rendering operational the Supreme State Control Authority (ASCE) and provichg
human and financial resources to enable it fully carry out its duties. Following the appointment of
its first officials charged with running it, regulatory measures wdl be taken to enhance its functions
and its attractiveness, takmg into account the general and technical inspectorates of the various
ministries. Government wdl also continue to enhance the transparency of the public finance
management system by makmg available on the website of the Ministry of the Economy and
Finance certain essential budgetary and accounting information In the same quest for
transparency, the supreme public finance control institution, namely, the State Au&t Office, has
pledged, as part of its action plan, to reduce the production time of its annual report and improve
its access to the public.

51. Government remains convinced that with the support of the World Bank, through the
Poverty Reduction Support Crecht, the satisfactory implementation of priority actions wdl help to
consolidate the macro-economic framework and sustain a stronger, healher and a more
sustainable economic growth necessary for a sipficant reduction of poverty.

52. Truly yours,



                                                       Jean-Ba~tisteM. P. COMPAORE
                                                      Commander of the National Order

     Annex 3: PRSC-8 support to the cotton sector and its impact on poverty alleviation


1.      The cotton sector has traditionally been important in Burkina Faso both for the economy
as a whole and for producers since roughly two and a half million people derive a significant
portion of their income from this sector. Over the past four years, the sector has gone through a
period of high operating costs and deficits, which were partly due to a misalignment between the
price received by farmers and the world market prices. Recent reforms in the sector resulted in
the application of a new pricing mechanism, which is designed to ensure a greater alignment
between producer and world cotton prices. The application of the new price mechanism by the
interprofession to the 2007-2008 campaign lowered cotton farm gate floor price fiom CFAF165
per kilo in 2006-2007 to CFAF145 per kilo in 2007-2008, which is equivalent to a 14 percent
price fall.

2.      The lower price partly contributed to the 33 percent reduction of cotton production, from
649,400tons in 200612007 to 434,000 tons in 200712008. However,the sharp decline was mostly
due to bad weather. The delays in payments to farmers for the previous season's crop, and the
late announcement of minimum producer prices, have also lowered farmers' interest in growing
cotton during the 200712008 campaign. As farmers reduced the acreage given over to cotton,
they expanded planting of cereal crops, such as maize, millet and sorghum. Bank Staff estimates
based on multipliers analysis show that a reduction in cotton production, if compensated by a
proportionate increase in food production, has little or no effect on aggregate output, value
added, household income, and poverty. Given a 25 percent fall in cotton production and a
proportionate compensation in food production, the analysis shows that aggregate production
falls marginally by 0.3 percent, whereas total value added and total household incomes increase
by 0.3 percent each. Consequently, the incidence of poverty remains essentially unchanged, with
a mere 0.2 percent drop.

3.      Overall, although the new price mechanism partly contributed to lower cotton production,
it also improved profitability prospects for the sector as a whole. Keeping the viability of the
cotton sector is essential, if the sector is to continue to play its vital role in increasing exports,
creating employment, ensuring food security, and reducing poverty in Burkina. With the
currently favorable outlook of cotton on the world markets, the strict application of the new
pricing mechanism will contribute to increase incomes received by farmers. Indeed, the world
cotton prices are on a recovery path, with current price levels significantly higher than the low
prices observed in 2005 and 2006 (Figure A3.1). Farmers stand to lose part of this price gain,
should the dollar continues to depreciate vis-a-vis the CFA franc, or should the world fertilizer
price increase pass through to farmers. On the plus side, Burkina Faso has authorized the
production of 15,000ha of Bt-cotton for the 200812009 campaign,with scale-up plans aiming for
national coverage within four years. Field trials show that the locally developed Bt-cotton offers
a dual cost reducing and yield increasing advantage to farmers. It can be hypothesized that the
positive price and technology effects will outweigh the negative exchange rate and input price
effects,resulting in a net income gains to farmers.

4.       We consider two scenarios in which cotton incomes are hypothesized to increase by 5
percent and 10 percent, respectively. The analysis is based on the Keynesian type multipliers
model based on a 2004 social accounting matrix (SAM) for Burkina Faso. The SAM contains 8
household groups, including cotton grower households. The cotton activity runs at two levels: at
the level of individual farms where household cotton producers produce cotton seeds, and at the
level of cotton companies (SOFITEX, SOCOMA, FASO COTON) where the cotton is ginned
and transformed into fiber. The ginned products are sold on the local and foreign markets, with
almost all the cotton fiber exported, while cotton seeds are used in the production of cotton seed
oil. Cotton oil is then used as a final household consumption good or as an intermediate input
used in the industry, especially the soap industry. The cotton sector clearly has key interactions
with the rest of the economy, and any injection of additional resources in cotton production leads
not only to an increase in the level of activity in this sector but also to a general rise in the level
of activity in the economy as a whole.

5.       The results in Table A3.1 show that a rise in the net cotton income has a relatively small
impact on the overall level of production and on the country's total GDP, but the impact on
employment seems stronger. Indeed, the total production and GDP increases from 0.1 percent (in the
case of a 5 percent increase in the net cotton income) to 0.2 percent when net income increases by 10
percent. Approximately 13.5 thousand additional jobs are created in the event of a 5 percent rise in
the net income of cotton growers. This figure exceeds 27 thousand new jobs if the net income of
cotton growers were to increase by 10 percent. These figures are based on the assumption that the
average level of wages will remain unchanged in the economy before and after the shock. If the wage
level were to rise, one would expect fewer gains in terms of job creation. The net cotton income

shock appears to have a relatively large effect on job creation because a boost in income affects the
entire economic system through intersectoral linkages of production and consumption.

   Table A3.1: Impact of an increase in the net income of cotton growers on the economy

6.       The impact on household incomes and poverty are shown in Figure A3.2. With a 0.3
percentage points decline in the poverty rate among cotton growers in response to a 10 percent
rise in net income, the effect on poverty reduction remains relatively small. Under the same
scenario, the incidence of poverty at the national level will drop marginally by 0.2 point
nationwide. At the same time, aggregate incomes of cotton growers grow by 1.6 percent, much
higher than the increase in average household income nationwide (0.2 percent).

Annex 4: Food Price Inflation in Burkina Faso and the Pro-poorness of Mitigating Policy
                                          Measures


 1. High levels of price increases since mid-2007. The nominal prices for selected food
    products strongly increased between January 2007 and January 2008, reaching up to 62% for
    shea oil (used for cooking in rural areas), 55% for white maize, and 50% for cotton oil. The
    prices of other heavily consumed cereals increased by 28% for sorghum and 12-14% for rice.
    Over the same period, the prices for salt and milk increased by 45% and 22%, respectively
    (Table A4.I).

 2. The second half of February 2008 has been marked by demonstrations over the high cost of
    living, stricter enforcement of customs duties, and increased licensing fees for street vendors.
    Demonstrations started in Bobo and three secondary cities on February 23, and spread to
    Ouagadougou on February 28.

 3. As a response to the demonstrations, the Government proposed on February 27 a temporary
    measure of import tax relief on products of mass consumption. According to the
    Government, the decision was reached after broad consultation with different socioeconomic
    groups, using the recommendations of a study aimed at reducing the impact of rising
    international prices on the cost of living. The temporary import duty relief measure will
    affect the following six products: rice, salt, pasta, sweet concentrated milk, powder milk, and
    infant milk; among the six products covered by the proposed policy measured, price increases
    vary from 45% for salt to 12-14% for rice, including a 13-22% change in milk prices, and a
    15-21% change in pasta-related products. For most of these products, the sharpest increases
    in prices occurred around November 2007 (Figure A4.1). The Government is also working
    with major companies that produce mass consumption products, such as sugar, soap and
    cooking oil. The goal of these consultations is to improve the alignment between the
    consumer price of these products with production and market conditions.

 4. The combined effects of price increases of several food items translated into high increases in
    food and non-alcoholic beverage price index, rising by more than 14% since January 2007.
    The increase in food prices more than doubles the level of price increase of other consumer's
    goods and services, including transportation, cleaning supplies and other goods and services
    (7% average price increase between January 2007 and January 2008). Because of the large
    weight of food products in total CPI (32%), the surge in food prices has strong effects on the
    general price level in the economy. Inflation is estimated at 6.9 percent from January 2007 to
    January 2008 (Table A4.2).

5.       Impacts of the Proposed Tax Subsidy on Consumer Prices.The transmission to the import
duty relief to consumers will depend on the pass-through rate. Preliminary estimates suggest that full
transmission of the tax break to consumers would erase or even reverse the recent surges in prices of
five out of the six products affected by the measure. Prices for pasta and powder milk would
marginally increase by 296, the prices for rice, concentrated milk and infant powder milk would fall
by 5-8%.        Salt price would remain high, even under the full pass-through scenario. But salt
consumption expenditure is marginal in total household budget, which would mitigate the impact of
the price increase on household total consumption.

6.       In practice, full price transmission is unlikely, due to leakages along the supply and
distribution chain of imported commodities. Partial pass-through is more likely, and assuming a 50%
pass-through rate, rice prices remain comparable to the 2007 levels; prices for infant powder and
concentrated milk increase marginally (3-4%), whereas pasta and powder milk prices rise by 11-
12%. In this scenario, the 2008 salt prices remain significantly higher and represent a 33% increase
with respect to 2007.

7.        Targeting Performance of the Proposed Tax Subsidy. The temporary elimination of
customs duties on rice, salt, pasta and milk products would amount to an estimated CFAF 6 billions
indirect transfers to economic agents, including households2'. This represents more than US$13.5
millions of forgone tax revenues for the Government over three months.22Assuming that a large
share of the tax subsidy is transferred to households via lower prices, it is useful to examine the
targeting performance of the transferred resources, particularly in terms of the benefits accruing to
the poor who are presumed to be the first beneficiaries of the policy measures.

8.        As noted above, not all tax subsidies are likely to be transmitted to households, poor and non-
poor. This is the first level of leakage to agents working along the supply and distribution chain of
subsidized products. The second source of leakage relates the low purchase rate among the poor, as
compared to the non poor households (Table A4.4). Since the subsidies are linked to purchase levels,
high-volume purchasers would benefit proportionally more from the intervention than low-volume
buyers. Poor households would tend to belong to the latter category. For milk for example, less than
5% of poor households purchased milk in 2003, compared to more than 18% for non poor
households. Similarly, 63% of non poor purchased rice in 2003, whereas only 40% of poor
household made such purchase in the same year.

9.       The low purchase rate, combined with low-volume consumption, results in a significantly
lower value of the consumption of the subsidized products by the poor. As a result, the import tax
subsidy does not appear to be perfectly targeted. The best performance is achieved with subsidies
targeting salt (Table A4.5). For each dollar of import tax subsidy received by the general population,
poor household receive 65 cents. This figure is significantly lower for milk (9 cents for each dollar),
pasta (29 cents), rice (31 cents), vegetable oil (36 cents) and soap (45 cents). Targeting performance
could be better in urban areas where purchasing rates tend to be higher (even for the poor). This
could be examined more thoroughly in follow-up assessments.

4. Key Messages and Perspectives

10.      Existing data confirm a substantial increase in prices of basic product over the past six
months. Prices of food items, such as maize and cooking oil, surged by more than 50% over the same
period. As a result, total inflation reached a record 7% between January 2007 and January 2008.
While underlying inflation remains low, prices of fresh and unprocessed food and energy rose much
faster, fueling the overall increases in price levels.

I I.     The Government's response to the food price crisis is to eliminate customs duties on basic
food products of mass consumption, including rice, salt, pasta, and milk products. Under a scenario
of a full pass-through to consumers, the tax subsidy will contribute to bringing prices back to their
2007 levels. Under the alternative partial pass-through scenario, the 2008 prices levels would be
lower (compared to the no-action scenario), but they would remain above the 2007 price levels.
Effective pass-through would require aggressive actions from Government price inspection services
so as to allow market forces to work to the benefit of consumers. Effective pass-through also depends
on ongoing dynamics in the world product and exchange rate markets, and these determinants need
to receive greater attention in subsequent analyses. Finally, effective and quick pass-through will
depend on how importers (particularly wholesalers) will price existing stocks.

12.      The analysis also reveals that the proposed measures are not perfectly targeted toward the
poor, but this is expected given the low purchase rate and low-volume consumption of the subsidized
items among the poor. Targeting performance is likely to be better among the urban poor, who tend
to be more directly affected by the price crisis.

13.      There are ongoing Government's actions on the ground with the goals to better assess the
situation, and propose concrete measures to improve the pass-through of the customs duty
elimination to consumer prices. Inquiry by the Staff at the Ministry of Commerce reveals: (i) the
Direction Ge'ne'rale des Affaires Economiques is currently leading field inspections on price
surveillance, so as to identify the real causes of recent price surges; (ii) In Ouagadougou, about 10
teams visited major wholesalers and collected prices; these wholesalers also supply Bobo Dioulasso;
(iii) a request has been sent to the Commission Nationale de la Concurrence, which is in charge of
competition and regulation; and (iv) a team of inspectors are on the field to investigate
noncompetitive practices.

14.      On the Bank's side, ongoing discussions focus on the possibility to bolster the Government's
capacity to respond to the shocks, through a series of interventions including direct budget support,
subsidized cotton inputs, and subsidized seeds in non-cotton zones. The package may also include
support to school lunch programs in the poorest zones.

                         Annex 5: PRSC-8 - Fund Relations Note




Press Release No. 081157                                       International Monetary Fund

FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE                                          Washington, D.C. 20431USA

July 1,2008



 IMF Executive Board CompletesSecond Review Under PRGF Arrangement with
              Burkina Faso and Approves US$6.5 Million Disbursement


The Executive Board of the International Monetary Fund (IMF) has completed the
second review of Burkina Faso's economicperformance under the three-year, SDR 15.05
million (about US$24.5 million) Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility (PRGF)
arrangement. The completion of the second review enables the release of an amount
equivalent to SDR 4.014 million (about US$6.5 million) bringing total disbursements
under the arrangement to SDR 8.02 million (about US$13 million).


In completing the review, the Board granted a waiver for the non-observance of a
performance criterion related to delays in sending automatic reminders to late filers and
nonfilers of tax returns, given that the substance of the measure has been achieved, and
other corrective steps are being taken.


The PRGF arrangement with Burkina Faso was approved on April 23, 2007 (see Press
Release No. 07/77)to support the government'seconomic reform program for 2007-10. On
January 9, 2008, an SDR 9.03 million (about US$14.7 million) increase in access was
approved to help address the impact of higher oil prices and the adverse shock to the
cotton sector (see Press Release No. 08/04).


Following the Executive Board's discussion, Mr. Takatoshi Kato, Deputy Managing
Director and Acting Chair, stated:


"In a difficult macroeconomic environment, the Burkinabk authorities' generally solid
macroeconomic policy performance has been commendable. With oil and food price
prices rising, the authorities' commitment to striking an appropriate balance in
maintaining economic and social stability is welcome.

"Fiscal policy that is in line with the targets set under the authorities' program has helped
preserve macroeconomic stability. Over time, it will be important to develop a well-
targeted social safety net to phase out short-term measures introduced in response to
quickly rising food prices. Improving debt sustainability will depend on a continued
reduction of fiscal deficits over the medium term.


"Consolidating progress in tax and customs administration and implementing a broad-
based tax policy reform will be key to achieving the authorities' medium-term revenue
targets. Mobilizing more revenue will help reduce fiscal deficits and preserve space for
poverty-reducing expenditures. To minimize budgetary risks, it will be important to
gradually close the gap between petroleum pump prices and prices mandated by the price
adjustmentmechanism.


"A number of planned structural reforms will help to set Burkina Faso's economy on a
sustainablehigh growth path. In the cotton sector, priorities include following-throughon
plans to find a strategic partner for the largest ginning company and improving
productivity of cotton production. In the financial sector, better managing financial risks
related to cotton financing, facilitating access to finance, and strengthening microfinance
supervisionwill be key," Mr. Kato said.

The PRGF is the IMF's concessional facility for low-income countries. PRGF loans carry
an annual interest rate of 0.5 percent and are repayable over 10 years with a 5%-year
grace period on principal payments.

                                  Annex 6: PRSC-8 - Burkina Faso
                       Joint Fund-World Bank Debt SustainabilityAnalysis


                            INTERNATIONAL MONETARY FUND AND
                       INTERNATIONAL DEVELOPMENT ASSOCIATION

                                            BURKINA FASO

                           Joint BanWFund Debt SustainabilityAnalysis

                 Prepared by the staffs of the International Development Association
                                 and the International Monetary Fund

                    Approved by Carlos A. Primo Braga and Sudhir Shetty (IDA)
                        and Thomas Krueger and Tessa van der Willigen (IMF)

                                               June 12,2008

Risks to the debt sustainability outlook have increased since theprevious debt
sustainabilityanalysis (DSA) update in December 2007. Following the reclassijkation of
Burkina Faso as a medium performer based on the World Bank's Country Policy and
Institutional Assessment (CPIA) rating, one indicative threshold (the NPV of debt-to-exports
ratio) is breached in the baseline scenario. This breach leads to a classijication of high risk
of debt distress.

            I.      EXTERNAL DEBT SUSTAINABILITYANALYSIS~~

                             A. WHATHASCHANGEDSINCETHE LASTD S A ? ~ ~

1.        Following a weaker rating in the World Bank's CPIA rating for 2006 and 2007,
Burkina Faso is now classified as a medium performer.In thejoint DSA from April 2007,
Burkina Faso was a strong performer based on the 2005 CPIA rating, and this classification
was maintained for the DSA update by Fund staff in December 2007. However, the average
CPIA rating for Burkina Faso for the period 2005-2007 has declined below the indicative
threshold for strong performers.25Consequently Burkina Faso has now to be reclassified as a
medium performer. The main causes for the decline in the CPIA ratings are a drop in 2006 of
both the debt policy rating and the transparency and accountability rating, by half a point
each.


23This DSA has been prepared jointly by staffs of the World Bank and Fund. The African Development Bank
participated in the DSA mission.

24For thejoint DSA from April 2007, see EBS/07/38, April 11,2007; for the DSA update from December 2007
prepared by Fund staff, see EBS/07/153, December 21,2007. The comparison to changes since the last DSA
refers to the December 2007 update, unless otherwise indicated.
25Results for the 2006 CPIA rating became available in summer 2006; the 2006 rating was 3.69, below the
threshold of 3.75 for strong           Results for the 2007 CPIA rating, as well as the 3-year average over
2005-07, also point to a medium policy performance.

2.        The reclassification to medium performer implies lower indicativethresholds for
debt indicators in the DSF. This is particularly relevant for the NPV of debt-to-exports
ratio, for which the baseline projectionnow breaches the indicative threshold starting in
2013. For other debt indicators, baseline projections and some stress tests remain well below
their indicativethresholds.

3.        The medium-term export outlook has been revised upwards (Figure1.1,Panel 1)
relative to projections in the DSA update from December 2007, mostly because of two
factors:26

                   Higher commodity prices:Gold prices have increased by about 35 percent in
                   US dollars and about 25 percent in euro-terms; this has a significanteffect on
                   export projections because of the start-up of large commercial gold mining
                   operations beginning in 2008.

                   Reassessment of medium-term export potential: the most significant
                   change is an upward revision for medium-term cotton exports, based on
                   sector-specific World Bank input, which reflects a rebound to pre-crisis level
                   in cotton output followed by gradual productivity improvements due to the
                   introduction of higher-yield GM cotton seeds, better storage facilities,and
                   advanced agriculturaltechniques (Figure I.1, Panel 2). Due to the constrained
                   availability of arable lands, the share of cotton exports in percent of GDP is
                   projected to decline markedly over the long-term (Figure I.1,Panel 3).
                   Compared to the relatively stable export-to-GDP ratio in the previous DSA,
                   the overall export-to-GDPprofile is now hump-shaped. The peak in 2015
                   arises because of a strong expansion in the mining sector and a rebound in the
                   cotton sector; in the long-run, the role of both sectors declines in percent of
                   GDP, while other sectors, like services, livestock and light manufacturing,
                   gradually increase in significance.




26The definition of service exports has been aligned with conventions in the Balance of Payments Manual, Fifth
Edition; in contrast to the previous definition, the Fifth Edition treats the income account (formerly classified as
factor services) separately from the service account. As a result, exports of services are now somewhat smaller
than had been previously the case. This accounts for the downward revision of historical data shown in
Figure I.1.

4.         The fiscal path is broadly unchanged. Externally-financedcapital expendituresin
2007 remained below expectations, leading to a modest downward revision in the following
years and correspondinglylower borrowing requirements. Fiscal targets were otherwise
maintained, with a long-run fiscal deficit target of about 2.5 percent of GDP (Figure I.1,
Panel 4).

5.         The debt database has been updated and reconciledwith creditor statements,
but this has not led to a major revision in the NPV of debt. The debt database has been
updated to reflect the debt stock outstanding as of end-2007; the reconciliation with available
creditor statementswas donejointly by staffs of the African Development Bank, the Fund,
and the World Bank. The resulting change in the estimated NPV of debt is small-for                                               2007,
it has been revised upwards by about 3.75 percent, whereas the average revision for 2007-25
is approximately -0.5 percent.

6.         The lower DSF thresholds signal a higher risk of debt distress (Figure 1.2). With
few changes in the macroeconomic framework,the path for most DSF indicators is close to
previous projections. The country's risk of debt distress, however, has increased because all

DSF indicatorsare now closer to their respective thresholds than was previouslythe case and
the NPV of debt-to-exports ratio even breaches its threshold.

                                   B. ASSESSING    VULNERABILITIES


7.      This section explores the vulnerability of the debt sustainability outlook to lower
export and growth assumptions and maintaining the current fiscal stance.

8.      A worse-than-expected export and growth performance is a clear risk, but
simulations show that most DSF indicators are relatively robust to more unfavorable
export and growth scenarios, with the exception of the NPV of debt-to-exports ratio.
The baseline scenario of the DSA assumes (i) a rapid cotton production rebound to pre-crisis
levels, and (ii) much higher gold prices in line with WE0 projections. The country-specific
alternative scenario in Figure 1.3 relaxes both assumptions and lowers the GDP growth rate,
while maintaining the path for the overall fiscal deficit in percent of GDP. The impact on
most debt sustainability indicators is modest, with baseline projections remaining below their
indicativethresholds for medium performers (Figure 1.4).The exception is the NPV of debt-
to-exportsratio, which breaches the threshold.

9.      A key factor for the resilience of most debt indicators to the adverse export and
growth shock is the assumption that the fiscal deficit declines throughout the projection
period as programmed in the baseline. This implicitly assumes that (i) structuralreforms in
the area of tax administration and fiscal policy would be implemented and (ii) that fiscal
tightening would be adopted as a response to permanent losses of revenue.

10.     If the fiscal deficit remains at the level observed over the past few years, debt
sustainability will be at risk. In a second country-specificscenario, growth and exports
followthe same trend as in the baseline, but fiscal policy is less tight, with the overall fiscal
deficit-to-GDPratio remaining in the long-run at about 4.5 percent of GDP, vs. 2.5 percent of
GDP in the baseline (Figure 1.5).This scenario leads to an upward trend in all debt
indicators, and a number of indicativethresholds would be breached. Besides increasingthe
risk of debt distress, the economy would become much more vulnerable to negative external
shocks,and there would be little room for implementingcounter-cyclicalpolicies.

11.     The risk of debt distress is high because one indicative threshold is breached in
the baseline projection: the threshold for the NPV of debt-to-exports ratio. The peak
ratio of about 190percent in the baseline projection of the NPV of debt-to-exports ratio is
well above the 150percent threshold. Under DSF guidelines,such a breach warrants a
classificationof high risk of debt distress, althoughthe GDP- and revenue-based DSF
indicatorsremain well below their indicative thresholds, including some of the alternative
scenariosand stresstests.

12.     There are a number of other positive factors as well as some downside risks:

Positivefactors

            Outstandingpayment record: since the transition from a centralized to a market-
            oriented economy in the early 1990s,Burkina Faso's government has consistently
            demonstrated its commitmentto stay current on its external payment obligations.
            This includes the period before the country benefited from debt relief under the
            Heavily Indebted Poor Country Initiative (HIPC), when the NPV of debt-to-
            exports ratio was well above 200 percent. Despite a high debt burden, the
            government even reduced outstandingexternalpayment arrears in these years.
            Given this demonstrated payment record, it appears unlikely that the government
            will fail to service its debt obligations.Moreover, the debt service ratios are
            projected to remain low throughout the entire projection period.

            Additional grant financing:this could improve the debt sustainability outlook
            significantly.The share of grant financing excluding IDA and AFD has increased
            in recent years to about 55 percent, whereas DSA projections are based on a more
            conservative 50 percent grant-financingshare. Raising the grant-financing share
            to 55 percent in the projection period would lower the peak NPV of debt-to-
            exports ratio by about 20 percentage points, but it would still remain above the
            indicativethreshold.

            Improvements in debt management:the authorities have recently adopted a
            national debt policy and are currentlyreceiving technical assistance in this area
            from the World Bank. Preliminary conclusions from the Debt Management
            PerformanceAssessment (DEMPA) indicatethat Burkina Faso has relatively
            strong controls for the contracting of external debt. The 35 percent
            concessionalityfloor is strictly enforced for all central-governmentforeign-
            currency borrowings, and projects are consistently scrutinized by a National
            Public Debt Committee before negotiations are concluded. A debt strategy that is
           planned to be added as an annex to the 2009 budget is being finalized and will
            include a ceiling on new borrowings based on the analysis of debt sustainability.
           While the evaluation also identifies a number of areas that do not meet the

             minimum requirements set out in the DeMPA framework (overstretching of the
             Public Debt National Committee,poor information on disbursements, poor
             dissemination on debt data, and weak audit institutions with respect to external
             borrowing), in many cases the improvements required for reaching those
             standards are relatively modest.

Downside risks

             Delayed fiscal adiustment: this poses a significantdownside risk, because without
             deficit reduction Burkina Faso's debt burden could eventually become
             unsustainable, even measured relative to GDP or revenue. Preventing this will
             require a stronger revenue effort, which in turn depends on further efforts in
             strengtheningtax and customs administration,and on implementing substantial
             tax policy reform.

             Adverse export shocks: these shocks would mostly affect the export-based debt
             indicators, whereas the other indicatorsare relatively robust with respect to this
             type of shock. Given that Burkina Faso is unlikely to have problems mobilizing
             foreign exchange to service its public debt27,the impact of this type of shock on
             the risk of debt distress is limited.

13.     In sum, there are significant up- and downside-risks. The most significant
downside risk is delayed fiscal adjustment, in which case the NPV of debt-to-exportsratio
could climb above 300 percent (Figure 1.5).However, even under this dire scenario a debt
default may not be the most likely outcomebecause (i) additional grants, particularly those
related to the IDAIAFD grant allocation mechanism, would mitigate the increase in debt
ratios, and (ii) the authorities have proven their commitment in the past to stay current on
their debt allocations even when the debt burden is high.

               11.       FISCAL DEBT SUSTAINABILITY ANALYSIS

14.     The results for the fiscal DSA are broadly similar to those of the external DSA.
Failure to reduce the current fiscal deficits would lead to ever-increasing debt indicators,
which is clearly unsustainable. The domestic debt stock is low-gross         domestic debt is
estimated at approximately 3.5 percent of GDP at end-2007, and net debt at 0.5 percent of
GDP; consequently,the baseline scenariosfor external and total public debt are similar.The
alternative scenarios in the fiscal DSA, though, differ in exploring the impact of different
fiscal policies on the debt sustainability outlook. For example, the 'no-reform' scenario,
which maintains the 2008 primary deficit of 5 percent of GDP over the projection horizon,
reinforces the result above (Figure 1.7).




27Burkina Faso's membership in the West African Economic and Monetary Union (WAEMU) gives it access to
the union's pool of foreign exchange reserves.

                                   111.    CONCLUSION

15.   Burkina Faso's risk of debt distress is high on account of the NPV of debt-to-
exports ratio; all other debt indicators are comfortablybelow their policy-dependent
thresholds under the baseline scenario. The overall deterioration from the previous DSA
suggeststhat more emphasis needs to be given to a prudent fiscal policy, to external
borrowing limited to concessional loans, and to a continued build-up in public debt
management capacity.
